The fuel tank inerting system features air-separation modules to generate nitrogen-enriched air to reduce the flammability of fuel vapour in the tanks. Parker also provides hydraulic power generation and distribution system: reservoirs, manifolds, accumulators, thermal control, isolation, software and new engine- and electric motor-driven pump designs. Parker estimates the contracts will generate more than $2&#160;billion in revenues over the life of the programme.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Variants">Variants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Variants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A350_variant_sizes.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/A350_variant_sizes.svg/220px-A350_variant_sizes.svg.png" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/A350_variant_sizes.svg/330px-A350_variant_sizes.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/A350_variant_sizes.svg/440px-A350_variant_sizes.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A350_variant_sizes.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Comparative lengths of the three variants, with the now cancelled -800.</div></div></div>\n<p>The three main variants of the A350 were launched in 2006, with entry into service planned for 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-eads_pr_20061201_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eads_pr_20061201-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> At the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">Paris Air Show</a>, Airbus postponed the entry into service of the A350-1000 by two years to mid-2017.<sup id="cite_ref-PARIS_A350-1000_delayed_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PARIS_A350-1000_delayed-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In July 2012, the A350\'s entry into service was delayed to the second half of 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_-1000_2012_delay_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_-1000_2012_delay-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> before the -900 began service on 15 January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-15_Jan_2015_EIS_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15_Jan_2015_EIS-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In October 2012, the -800 was due to enter service in mid-2016,<sup id="cite_ref-FG23Oct2012_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG23Oct2012-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> but its development has been cancelled since September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-FG140917_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG140917-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The A350 is also offered as the ACJ350 corporate jet by <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Corporate_Jets" title="Airbus Corporate Jets">Airbus Corporate Jets</a> (ACJ), offering a 20,000&#160;km (10,800&#160;nmi) range for 25 passengers for the -900 derivative.<sup id="cite_ref-ACJ350_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACJ350-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A350-900">A350-900</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: A350-900">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The A350-900 is the first A350 model, has a <a href="/wiki/Maximum_takeoff_weight" title="Maximum takeoff weight">maximum takeoff weight</a> (MTOW) of 280 tonnes, typically seats 325 passengers, and has a range of 8,100&#160;nmi (15,001&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-A350-900_specs_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A350-900_specs-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Airbus says that per seat, the Boeing 777-200ER should have a 16 percent heavier <a href="/wiki/Manufacturer%27s_empty_weight" title="Manufacturer&#39;s empty weight">manufacturer\'s empty weight</a>, a 30 percent higher block fuel consumption, and 25 percent higher cash operating costs than the A350-900.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The \xe2\x88\x92900 is designed to compete with the Boeing 777 and 787<sup id="cite_ref-ser_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ser-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> (777-200ER/<a href="/wiki/Boeing_777#777-200LR" title="Boeing 777">LR</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777#777-8" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777-8</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner#787-10" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787-10</a>), while replacing the Airbus <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340#A340-300" title="Airbus A340">A340-300</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340#A340-500" title="Airbus A340">A340-500</a>.\n</p><p>A proposed A350\xe2\x88\x92900R extended-range variant was to feature the higher engine thrust, strengthened structure, and landing gear of the 308 tonnes MTOW -1000 to give a further 800&#160;nmi (1,500&#160;km) range.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> \nAn A350\xe2\x88\x92900F freighter with a 5,000&#160;nmi (9,260&#160;km) range and a similar payload and volume to the 91.7 tonne and 440&#160;m<sup>3</sup> (16,000&#160;cu&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-11" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-11">McDonnell Douglas MD-11F</a> should be studied after the -1000 is done, depending on market demand.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Philippine_Airlines" title="Philippine Airlines">Philippine Airlines</a> will replace its A340-300 with an A350-900HGW<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> high gross weight version available from 2017. It will enable non-stop Manila-New York City flights without payload limitations in either direction,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> a 7,404&#160;nmi (13,712&#160;km) flight.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> The PAL version will have a 278 tonne MTOW, and from 2020, the -900 will be proposed with the ULR\'s 280 tonne MTOW, up from the 268 tonnes for the original weight variant and the certified 260, 272, and 275 tonne variants, with the large fuel capacity. This will enable a 8,100&#160;nmi (15,001&#160;km) range with 325 seats in a three-class layout.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FIN_A350_OH-LWA_7oct15_LFBO-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/FIN_A350_OH-LWA_7oct15_LFBO-2.jpg/220px-FIN_A350_OH-LWA_7oct15_LFBO-2.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/FIN_A350_OH-LWA_7oct15_LFBO-2.jpg/330px-FIN_A350_OH-LWA_7oct15_LFBO-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/FIN_A350_OH-LWA_7oct15_LFBO-2.jpg/440px-FIN_A350_OH-LWA_7oct15_LFBO-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1483" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FIN_A350_OH-LWA_7oct15_LFBO-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">Finnair</a> A350-900</div></div></div>\n<p>In early November 2017, Emirates committed to purchase 40 Boeing 787-10 aircraft before Airbus presented a picture-changing A350-900 layout with the rear pressure bulkhead pushed back by 2.5&#160;ft (1&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek14nov2017_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek14nov2017-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> After Emirates\' <a href="/wiki/Tim_Clark_(airline_executive)" title="Tim Clark (airline executive)">Tim Clark</a> was shown a ten-abreast economy cabin and galley changes, he said the -900 is "more marketable" as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The average lease rates of the first A350-900s produced in 2014 were $1.1 million per month, not including maintenance reserves amounting to $18 million after 10\xe2\x80\x9312 years, and falling to $940,000 per month in 2018 while a new A350-900 is leased for $1.2 million per month and its interior can cost $12 million, 10% of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="A350-900ULR">A350-900ULR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: A350-900ULR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20180403_A350-XWB-ULR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/20180403_A350-XWB-ULR.jpg/220px-20180403_A350-XWB-ULR.jpg" width="220" height="96" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/20180403_A350-XWB-ULR.jpg/330px-20180403_A350-XWB-ULR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/20180403_A350-XWB-ULR.jpg/440px-20180403_A350-XWB-ULR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4878" data-file-height="2121" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20180403_A350-XWB-ULR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First A350-900ULR before being painted in <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> livery</div></div></div>\n<p>The MTOW of the ultra-long range -900ULR is being increased to 280&#160;t (620,000&#160;lb) and its fuel capacity from 141,000 to 165,000&#160;l (37,000 to 44,000&#160;US&#160;gal) within existing fuel tanks, enabling up to 19-hour flights with a 9,700&#160;nmi (18,000&#160;km) range.<sup id="cite_ref-FG170510_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG170510-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>  The MTOW is increased by 5 tonnes from the previously certified 275 tonnes variant.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Because the A350-900\'s fuel consumption is 5.8 tonnes/hour, it needs an additional 24 tonnes of fuel to fly 19 hours instead of the standard 15 hours: the increased MTOW and lower payloads will enable the larger fuel capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>  Non-stop flights could last more than 20 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>  The first \xe2\x88\x92900ULR was rolled out without its engines in February 2018 for ground testing, and debuted flight-tests after engine installation to check the larger fuel capacity and to measure the performance improvements from the extended <a href="/wiki/Winglet" class="mw-redirect" title="Winglet">winglets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>  It made its first flight on 23 April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a>, the launch customer, will use its seven -900ULR aircraft on <a href="/wiki/Non-stop_flight" title="Non-stop flight">non-stop flights</a> between Singapore and New York City, and cities on the U.S. west coast.<sup id="cite_ref-ulr_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ulr-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>  Singapore Airlines\' seating is to be from 170 in largely business class seating up to over 250 in mixed seating.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The planes can be reconfigured.<sup id="cite_ref-ausbtulr_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ausbtulr-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> They will have two seating classes, but they were not specified as of November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The airline received its first -900ULR on 23 September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Air_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Dubai Air Show">Dubai Air Show</a>, Airbus\'s John Leahy noted the appetite of the Middle East gulf airlines for this variant.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In February 2018, Qatar Airways expressed no interest in the -900ULR.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ACJ350">ACJ350</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: ACJ350">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Airbus\' corporate jet version of the A350, the ACJ350, is derived from the A350-900ULR. As a result of the increased fuel capacity from the -900ULR, the ACJ350 has a maximum range of 20,000&#160;km (10,800&#160;nmi).<sup id="cite_ref-acj350_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acj350-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="A350_Regional">A350 Regional</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: A350 Regional">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After the Boeing 787-10 launch at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">Paris Air Show</a>, Airbus discussed with airlines a possible A350-900 Regional with a reduced MTOW of 250 tonnes and engine thrust reduced to 70,000-75,000&#160;lb (from the standard 85,000&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-359reg_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359reg-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>  The variant was said to be optimized for routes up to 6,800&#160;nmi (12,594&#160;km) with seating for up to 360 passengers in a single-class layout.<sup id="cite_ref-359reg_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359reg-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Etihad Airways and Singapore Airlines were said to be ordering the A350 Regional.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Since 2013, there has been no further announcement about this variant.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A350-1000">A350-1000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: A350-1000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EGLF_-_Airbus_A350_-_F-WLXV_(43447425601).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EGLF_-_Airbus_A350_-_F-WLXV_%2843447425601%29.jpg/220px-EGLF_-_Airbus_A350_-_F-WLXV_%2843447425601%29.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EGLF_-_Airbus_A350_-_F-WLXV_%2843447425601%29.jpg/330px-EGLF_-_Airbus_A350_-_F-WLXV_%2843447425601%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EGLF_-_Airbus_A350_-_F-WLXV_%2843447425601%29.jpg/440px-EGLF_-_Airbus_A350_-_F-WLXV_%2843447425601%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5085" data-file-height="3516" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EGLF_-_Airbus_A350_-_F-WLXV_(43447425601).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airbus A350-1000 prototype</div></div></div>\n<p>The A350-1000 is the largest variant of the A350 family at just under 74 metres in length. It seats 366 passengers in a typical three-class layout with a range of 8,000&#160;nmi (14,800&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-150925PR_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150925PR-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> With a 9-abreast configuration, it is designed to replace the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340" title="Airbus A340">Airbus A340</a>-600 and compete with the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-300ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-300ER">Boeing 777-300ER</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777X" title="Boeing 777X">777-9</a>. Airbus estimates a 366-seat -1000 should have a 35 t lighter <a href="/wiki/Operating_empty_weight" title="Operating empty weight">operating empty weight</a> than a 398-seat 777-9, a 15% lower trip cost, a 7% lower seat cost, and a 400&#160;nmi (740&#160;km) greater range.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Compared to a Boeing 777-300ER with 360 seats, Airbus claims a 25% <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_aircraft" title="Fuel economy in aircraft">fuel burn per seat</a> advantage for an A350-1000 with 369 seats.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>  The 7&#160;m (23&#160;ft) extension seats 40 more passengers with 40% more premium area.<sup id="cite_ref-1611pres_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1611pres-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\nThe -1000 can match the 40 more seats of the 777-9 by going 10-abreast but with diminished comfort.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The A350-1000 has an 11-frame stretch over the \xe2\x88\x92900 and a slightly larger wing than the \xe2\x88\x92800/900 models with trailing-edge extension increasing its area by 4%. This will extend the high-lift devices and the ailerons, making the chord bigger by around 400&#160;mm, optimising flap lift performance as well as cruise performance.<sup id="cite_ref-FG100423_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG100423-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The main <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a> is a 6-wheel bogie instead of a 4-wheel bogie, put in a one frame longer bay.  The <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Trent_XWB" title="Rolls-Royce Trent XWB">Rolls-Royce Trent XWB</a> engine\'s thrust is augmented to 97,000&#160;lbf (430&#160;kN).<sup id="cite_ref-ACU150122_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACU150122-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> These and other engineering upgrades are necessary so that the \xe2\x88\x921000 model maintains range.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, Airbus redesigned the A350-1000 with higher weights and a more powerful engine variant for more range for trans-Pacific operations which will boost its appeal to <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a>, Singapore Airlines, which committed to 20 777-9, and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>, which could turn to 777-300ERs to replace its 747-400s. Emirates was disappointed with the changes and cancelled its order for 50 A350-900s and 20 A350-1000s instead of citing the whole order to the larger variant.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight20mar2017_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight20mar2017-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Assembly of the first fuselage major components started in September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-150925PR_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150925PR-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In February 2016, final assembly started at the A350 Final Assembly Line in Toulouse.  Three flight test aircraft was planned with entry into service scheduled for mid-2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus10feb2016_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus10feb2016-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The first aircraft completed its body join on 15 April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Its maiden flight took place on 24 November 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-FG-1000FirstFlight_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG-1000FirstFlight-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The A350-1000 <a href="/wiki/Flight-test" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight-test">flight-test</a> programme planned for 1,600 flight hours; 600 hours on the first aircraft, MSN59, for the <a href="/wiki/Flight_envelope" title="Flight envelope">flight envelope</a>, systems and powerplant checks; 500 hours on MSN71 for cold and warm campaigns, <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a> checks and high-altitude tests; and 500 hours on MSN65 for route proving and <a href="/wiki/ETOPS" title="ETOPS">ETOPS</a> assessment, with an interior layout for cabin development and certification.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> In cruise at Mach&#160;0.854 (912&#160;km/h; 492&#160;kn) and 35,000&#160;ft, its fuel flow at 259&#160;t (571,000&#160;lb) is 6.8&#160;t (15,000&#160;lb) per hour within a 10,000&#160;km (5,400&#160;nm), 11 h 30 m early long test flight.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>  Flight tests allowed raising the <a href="/wiki/Maximum_Take-Off_Weight" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximum Take-Off Weight">Maximum Take-Off Weight</a> from 308 to 316&#160;t (679,000 to 697,000&#160;lb), the 8&#160;t (18,000&#160;lb) increase giving 450&#160;nmi (830&#160;km) more range.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>  Airbus then completed functional and reliability testing.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Type Certification was awarded by <a href="/wiki/EASA" class="mw-redirect" title="EASA">EASA</a> on 21 November 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-TCDS_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCDS-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> along <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a> certification. The first serial unit was on the final <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> in early December.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek21nov2017_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek21nov2017-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>  After its maiden flight on 7 December, delivery to launch customer Qatar Airways slipped to early 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The delay was due to issues with the business class seat installation.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>  It was delivered on 20 February<sup id="cite_ref-Flight20feb2018_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight20feb2018-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> and entered commercial service on Qatar Airways\' Doha to London Heathrow route on 24 February.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight24feb2018_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight24feb2018-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It features an automatic emergency <a href="/wiki/Descent_(aeronautics)" title="Descent (aeronautics)">descent</a> function to around 10,000&#160;ft (3,000&#160;m) and notifies <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a> if the crew fails to respond to an alert, indicating possible incapacitation from <a href="/wiki/Depressurisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Depressurisation">depressurisation</a>. The avionics software adaptation is activated by a push and pull button to avoid mistakes and could be retrofitted in the smaller -900.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight21nov2017_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight21nov2017-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>  All performance targets have been met or exceeded and it remains within its weight specification, unlike early \xe2\x88\x92900s.<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek21nov2017_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek21nov2017-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Its basic 308&#160;t (679,000&#160;lb) maximum take-off weight was bumped to 311&#160;t (686,000&#160;lb) before offering a possible 316&#160;t (697,000&#160;lb) version.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Its 316 t MTOW appeared in the 29 May 2018 update of its type certificate data sheet.<sup id="cite_ref-TCDS_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCDS-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\nThis raised its range from 7,950 to 8,400&#160;nmi (14,720 to 15,560&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-AvWeek14jun2018_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvWeek14jun2018-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\nA further MTOW increase by 3t to 319t is under study to be available from 2020 and could be a response to Qantas\' <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo_Route#Non-stop_flights" title="Kangaroo Route">Project Sunrise</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_stretch">Further stretch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Further stretch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Airbus has explored the possibility of a further stretch offering 45 more seats.<sup id="cite_ref-FG160229_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG160229-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> A potential 4&#160;m stretch would remain within the exit limit of four door pairs, and a modest MTOW increase from 308&#160;t to 319&#160;t would need only 3% more thrust, within the <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Trent_XWB" title="Rolls-Royce Trent XWB">Rolls-Royce Trent XWB</a>-97 capabilities, and would allow a 14,100&#160;km (7,600&#160;nmi) range to compete with the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777X" title="Boeing 777X">Boeing 777-9</a> capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This variant was to be a replacement for the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> tentatively dubbed the A350-8000,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> -2000<sup id="cite_ref-FG160603_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG160603-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> or -1100.<sup id="cite_ref-FG160229_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG160229-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Within the June 2016 Airbus Innovation Days, chief commercial officer <a href="/wiki/John_Leahy_(executive)" title="John Leahy (executive)">John Leahy</a> was concerned about the size of a 400-seat market besides the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8" title="Boeing 747-8">Boeing 747-8</a> and the 777-9 and chief executive <a href="/wiki/Fabrice_Br%C3%A9gier" title="Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier">Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier</a> feared such an aircraft could cannibalise demand for the -1000.<sup id="cite_ref-FG160603_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG160603-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The potential 79&#160;m-long (258&#160;ft) airplane was competing against a hypothetical <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777X#777-10X" title="Boeing 777X">777-10X</a> for Singapore Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>  At the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">Paris Air Show</a>, the concept was shelved for lacking market appeal and in January 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fabrice_Br%C3%A9gier" title="Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier">Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier</a> focused on enhancing the A350-900/1000 to capture potential before 2022/2023, when it will be possible to stretch the A350 with a new engine generation.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undeveloped_A350-800">Undeveloped A350-800</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Undeveloped A350-800">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 60.45&#160;m (198.3&#160;ft) long A350-800 was designed to seat 276 passengers in a typical 3-class configuration with a range of 15,270&#160;km (8,245&#160;nmi) with an MTOW of 259&#160;t (571,000&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus-Family-Figures_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus-Family-Figures-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2010 Airbus opted to develop the -800 as a shrink of the baseline -900, avoid a specific development and increasing its payload by 3&#160;t (6,600&#160;lb) or its range by 460&#160;km (250&#160;nmi) but leading to a fuel burn penalty by "a couple of percent" according to John Leahy.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The previously planned optimisation to the structure and landing gear was not beneficial enough against better <a href="/wiki/Commonality" class="mw-redirect" title="Commonality">commonality</a> and maximum takeoff weight increase by 11t from 248t.<sup id="cite_ref-flightglobal2_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flightglobal2-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The \xe2\x88\x92800\'s fuselage is 10 frames shorter (six forward and four aft of wing) than the \xe2\x88\x92900 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-FG_family_commonality_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG_family_commonality-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> It was designed to supplement the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330-200</a> long-range twin.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Airbus planned to decrease structural weight in the -800 as development continued, which should have been around airframe 20.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While its backlog reached 182 in mid-2008, it diminished since 2010 as customers switched to the larger -900.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> After launching the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330neo" title="Airbus A330neo">Airbus A330neo</a> at the 2014 Farnborough Airshow, Airbus dropped the A350-800, with its CEO <a href="/wiki/Fabrice_Br%C3%A9gier" title="Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier">Fabrice Br\xc3\xa9gier</a> saying "I believe all of our customers will either convert to the A350-900 or the A330neo".<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> He later confirmed at a September 2014 press conference that development of the A350-800 had been "cancelled."<sup id="cite_ref-FG140917_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG140917-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> There were 16 orders left for the -800 since <a href="/wiki/Yemenia" title="Yemenia">Yemenia</a> switched to the -900 and <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Airlines" title="Hawaiian Airlines">Hawaiian Airlines</a> moved to the A330neo in December 2014: 8 for <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a> and 8 for <a href="/wiki/Asiana_Airlines" title="Asiana Airlines">Asiana Airlines</a>, both also having orders for the -900.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, Aeroflot and Airbus announced the cancellation of its -800 order, leaving Asiana Airlines as the only customer for the variant.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> After the negotiation between Airbus and Asiana Airlines,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Asiana converted orders of eight A350-800s and one A350-1000 to nine A350-900s.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orders_and_deliveries">Orders and deliveries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Orders and deliveries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style 31&#160;August&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_O_D_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_O_D-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operators">Operators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Operators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathay_Pacific_A350-1000XWB_B-LXA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cathay_Pacific_A350-1000XWB_B-LXA.jpg/220px-Cathay_Pacific_A350-1000XWB_B-LXA.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cathay_Pacific_A350-1000XWB_B-LXA.jpg/330px-Cathay_Pacific_A350-1000XWB_B-LXA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Cathay_Pacific_A350-1000XWB_B-LXA.jpg/440px-Cathay_Pacific_A350-1000XWB_B-LXA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3078" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathay_Pacific_A350-1000XWB_B-LXA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> A350-1000 before landing. The airline is the second largest A350 operator after Qatar Airways.</div></div></div>\n<p>There were 193 A350 aircraft in service with 21 operators as of  31&#160;August&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A350_XWB&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_O_D_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_O_D-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:center; background:#fbf8db">\n\n<tbody><tr style="background:#cdf;">\n<th>Operator\n</th>\n<th>First commercial service\n</th>\n<th>Number in service\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Air_Cara%C3%AFbes" title="Air Cara\xc3\xafbes">Air Cara\xc3\xafbes</a></td>\n<td>2 March 2017<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>2\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Asiana_Airlines" title="Asiana Airlines">Asiana Airlines</a></td>\n<td>15 May 2017<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>6\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Air_Mauritius" title="Air
